<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">In this letter, we present a novel radio frequency identification (RFID) tag design optimized especially for the inkjet printing process. These tags are printed using narrow conductors, which enables low cost and fast manufacturing rate. We have manufactured such tag designs using three different line widths: 50, 125, and 200 μm. In this letter, we present the simulation and measurement results. We have also included a comparison between the novel narrow-line tag and a dipole-type commercial tag. Results are encouraging; the read range of the narrow-line tag is comparable to the read range of the commercial tag even though the commercial tag is made of copper, which has approximately two times higher conductivity than the silver ink used in this study. Moreover, the narrow-line tag antenna needs 83% less conductor surface area than the antenna geometry of the commercial tag. This means a significant drop in the manufacturing costs.</div>

In this paper, for the first time quadrate bowtie antennas with round corners [1] are realized and analyzed on paper substrate for UHF RFID tags. These inkjet printed antennas exhibit high performance which give freedom for their applications. Their area is smaller than the general triangle bowtie antenna and have adva...&quot;,&quot;pdfSize&quot;:&quot;495KB&quot;,&quot;openUrlImgLoc&quot;:&quot;http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/assets/img/btn.find-in-library.png&quot;},&quot;refType&quot;:&quot;biblio&quot;,&quot;id&quot;:&quot;ref3&quot;},{&quot;order&quot;:&quot;4&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;&lt;em&gt;Alien Higgs 3 product overview&lt;/em&gt;,  [online]  Available: http://www.alientechnology.com.&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;Alien Higgs 3 product overview&quot;,&quot;context&quot;:[{&quot;sec&quot;:&quot;sec2&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot; The IC used in the narrow-line tags is the Higgs 3 RFID chip manufactured by Alien Technology [4].&quot;,&quot;part&quot;:&quot;1&quot;}],&quot;refType&quot;:&quot;biblio&quot;,&quot;id&quot;:&quot;ref4&quot;},{&quot;order&quot;:&quot;5&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;&lt;em&gt;Ansoft High Frequency Structure Simulator HFSS&lt;/em&gt;,  [online]  Available: http://www.ansoft.com/products/hf/hfss/.&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;Ansoft High Frequency Structure Simulator, HFSS&quot;,&quot;context&quot;:[{&quot;sec&quot;:&quot;sec3&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;The narrow-line tag antennas were designed using Ansoft's High Frequency Structure Simulator (HFSS) [5].&quot;,&quot;part&quot;:&quot;1&quot;}],&quot;refType&quot;:&quot;biblio&quot;,&quot;id&quot;:&quot;ref5&quot;},{&quot;order&quot;:&quot;6&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;T. <div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Additive manufacturing methods of electronics such as inkjet, screen gravure, and flexo printing methods—i.e., printable electronics—promise to lower the overall manufacturing costs by more efficient use of materials. Thus, printable electronics has the potential to aid the global adoption of radio frequency identification (RFID) by lowering the production costs of a single RFID tag <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. In addition, printable electronics also allows the RFID tag antenna to be printed directly on the product package.</p><p>Nowadays, researchers all around the world are developing cost-effective inkjet-printable RFID tags <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. In this letter, we present a novel inkjet-printed tag antenna design to lower the overall manufacturing costs by minimizing the build time and the amount of silver ink required in the fabrication process.</p><p>The tag design presented in this letter is formed using very narrow and thin conductors. The use of such conductors dramatically reduces the amount of silver ink needed to fabricate a tag. Furthermore, these kinds of conductor lines are ideal for the highly accurate digital printing process, which enables fast printing speeds and high yield.</p><p>Despite its extremely small conductor area and thus low cost, the narrow wire tag has the performance to meet the needs of many applications.</p><p>The narrow-line tags are printed using three different line widths: 50, 125, and 200 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m. Each of these three versions were also printed using four different conductor thicknesses, from 1.5 to 6 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-4" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m, to allow us to see the effect of the conductor thickness on the performance as well.</p><p>This letter presents the novel narrow-line RFID tag design, its simulation and measurement results, as well as a comparison against a commercial tag design.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Tag Structure</h2></div><p>The narrow-line tags are composed of a folded half-wavelength dipole antenna and an integrated circuit (IC) on a strap. The printing layout and the key dimensions of a narrow-line tag are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. The footprint dimensions of the tag are 10 (L) ×1 (W) cm<sup>2</sup>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5462926/5462926-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5462926/5462926-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Geometry and the key dimensional parameters of the passive narrow-line RFID tag.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5462926/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The antenna was formed using 50-, 125-, and 200-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-7" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m-wide printed conductors. The conductors were formed on 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-10" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-11" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m-thick Kapton polyimide film by printing one to four layers of Harima NPS-J HP silver ink, which has a conductivity of 33 MS/m, using and iTi XY MDS 2.0 inkjet printer equipped with Spectra S-class printheads. The IC used in the narrow-line tags is the Higgs 3 RFID chip manufactured by Alien Technology <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_2">[4]</a>.</p><p>The printing resolution was set to 600 dpi, which was found optimal for the given ink, drop volume, and substrate. An example of the printed samples is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5462926/5462926-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5462926/5462926-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>One example of the fabricated narrow-line tag samples with the IC attached using conductive epoxy.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5462926/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Simulation Results</h2></div><p>The narrow-line tag antennas were designed using Ansoft's High Frequency Structure Simulator (HFSS) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_3">[5]</a>. The antenna impedance is conjugate-matched to the H3 chip impedance using the parallel equivalent RC-circuit from the manufacturer's datasheet (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-13" role="math" style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">Z_{\rm S}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-207" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.264em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.14em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-208" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-209" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-210" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/005A.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-211" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-212" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-213" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/004C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">Z_{\rm L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively. This ratio is known as the power reflection coefficient, and it describes the quality of power matching between two complex impedances. In the present study, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-214" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-215" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-216" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0393.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">\Gamma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is used to predict the power delivery to the IC according to the simulated tag antenna impedance.</p><p>Simulated <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-217" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-218" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-219" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0393.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">\Gamma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for tags with 1.5 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-220" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-221" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-222" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m conductor thickness and different line widths are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>, and according to the results, the tag antennas are well matched with better than −5.3 dB power reflection coefficient throughout the frequencies of interest. This means that at least 70% of the available power is delivered to the IC.

Realized gain includes the losses caused by conductors with finite conductivity and the possible power reflections caused by impedance mismatches between the antenna and the generator. Hence, the realized gain <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-233" role="math" style="display: inline-block; As expected, decreasing the line width and conductor thickness increases the conductor loss in the antenna structure through the skin effect and thus lowers the realized gain of the tag. The results predict that the realized gains of the tags increase as a function of line width and thickness at all studied frequencies.

<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Measurement Results</h2></div><p>The measurements were carried out in a compact anechoic cabinet using a frequency range from 800 MHz to 1 GHz with 0.5-MHz steps. The used transmit power ranged from 0 to 27 dBm with 0.1-dB steps, and measurement distance was 0.45 m.</p><p>The primary measurement, measured with the Tagformance system <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_4">[9]</a>, threshold power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-310" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.444em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-311" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-312" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-313" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0050.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.117em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-314" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-315" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-316" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0074.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-317" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0078.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 6px; height: 5px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; Based on the tag's threshold power, we are able to calculate the realized gain <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-318" role="math" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0078.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 6px; height: 5px; vertical-align: 0px; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> stands for the corresponding threshold level measured at a certain frequency point during the threshold power sweep. Measured realized gains for each tag version are shown in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>.</p><p>One can see that the realized gain increases quickly as the conductor thickness and width are increased. This is caused by the decrease in ohmic losses in the printed conductors. Furthermore, one can see the differences between simulated and measured values of realized gains. This is due to the difficulty of modeling losses in the thin and narrow silver ink conductors.</p><p>The theoretical read range describes the maximum distance at which the read operation is still working, assuming free-space conditions. The narrow-line tag using 200 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-475" role="math" style="display: inline-block; The narrow-line tag with 125-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-481" role="math" style="display: inline-block; </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5462926/5462926-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5462926/5462926-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Theoretical read range results for the measured narrow line tag samples.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5462926/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The thickness of the conductors is more vital for the 125-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-487" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-491" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-492" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; The performance of these tags continues to increase as more ink layers are added. The widest narrow-line tag samples, tags with 200-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-493" role="math" style="display: inline-block; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-494" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-495" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m-wide conductors, do not seem to benefit from the added conductor thickness after thickness of 3.0 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-496" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-497" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-498" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m.</p><p>Interestingly, the narrow-line tag using 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-499" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-500" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-501" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m line width with an estimated conductor thickness of 6.0 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-502" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-503" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-504" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m has a longer read range than the narrow-line tag using 125 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-505" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-506" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-507" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m line width at frequency ranges 800–870 MHz. This is explained by the better impedance matching of the 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-508" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-509" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-510" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m at this particular frequency range.</p><p>One should also note the wide bandwidth of the narrow-line tags, i.e., flatness of the read-range curve.</p><p>For example, the 200-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-511" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-512" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-513" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m narrow-line tag has a 100-MHz bandwidth of almost flat maximum read range. This will easily cover the European and U.S. RFID bands with additional impedance tuning.</p><p>There is a difference between the simulation results and measurement results in terms of the best operation frequency band. This is caused by the fact that the modeling of the tag antenna's impedance is challenging. This is mainly due to the very thin, uneven, and porous silver ink conductor material.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Comparison against a Commercial Tag</h2></div><p>To show the promising performance of the narrow-line tag design, this section presents a read-range comparison against a commercial tag <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_5">[11]</a>, which represents a high-performance dipole RFID tag. The narrow-line tag geometry requires almost six times of 83% less conductor surface area than the geometry of the commercial tag.</p><p>The commercial tag is also equipped with the Alien Higgs 3 chip. The commercial design is fabricated of copper, which has a conductivity of 59.6 MS/m versus the 33 MS/m conductivity of the silver ink. Hence, the use of silver ink produces more ohmic losses, increasing the power needed to activate the tag and reducing the read range. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a> presents the acquired read-range results to compare the performances of the narrow-line tag using a line width of 200 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-514" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-515" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-516" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m with a conductor thickness of 4.5 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-517" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-518" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-519" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m and the commercial tag.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5462926/5462926-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5462926/5462926-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Read-range comparison against the reference tag design.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5462926/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>One can see from the results that the narrow-line tag design falls behind the commercial tag by approximately 3 m in peak read range. At the European band (866 MHz), the read-range difference is about 5 m, while at the U.S. band (915 MHz), the difference is small, less than 1 m. At the Asian band (954 MHz), the read-range difference is approximately 2 m. As for now, the narrow-line tag cannot yet match the performance of the commercial tag; this fact illustrates the tradeoff when using narrow and thin conductors. However, considering that the reference tag has much thicker, wider, and better conducting copper conductors acting as the radiating elements, the performance of the narrow-line tag can be considered very good.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>This letter presents a novel inkjet-printable RFID tag antenna design using extremely narrow conductors. The results are promising; the maximum read range was slightly over 7 m with the narrow-line tag using 200-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-520" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-521" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-522" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">\mu</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m-wide conductor traces. Our comparison shows that the performance of the narrow-line tag is comparable to commercial copper fabricated tags.</p><p>Our purpose was to present a new alternative way to lower the manufacturing costs of inkjet-printed RFID tags by using very few conductive materials. Compared to the commercial tag design, the surface area of needed conductor material to form the tag antenna is decreased by 83%.</p><p>Furthermore, due to the properties of the digital inkjet printing process, this kind of printable structure with narrow lines is fast to print out.</p><p>Future development is aimed to optimize the design to allow further read ranges. Also, we are striving to increase the bandwidth of the narrow-line tag even more by additional tuning of the impedance matching network. Moreover, we will conduct studies on the effects of the materials under identification to the performance of the narrow-line tags.</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGMENT</h3><p>The authors would like to thank Dr. K. Kaija and Dr. T. Joutsenoja for manufacturing the printed narrow-line tag antenna samples.</p></div></div>

	<!-- ngIf: !vm.loading.relatedArticles --><!-- ngInclude: getContextUrl() --><div ng-include="getContextUrl()" class="u-mt-2 ng-scope" ng-if="!vm.loading.relatedArticles" article-number="5462926" context="related-articles" context-data="vm.data.relatedArticles"><section id="fullTextRelatedArticles" class="document-all-related-articles ng-scope">
	<h2 class="document-ft-section-header">Related Articles</h2>
	
	<!-- ngIf: !vm.contextData.similar.length -->
	
	<!-- ngIf: vm.contextData.similar.length --><div class="stats-document-relatedArticles ng-scope" ng-if="vm.contextData.similar.length">
		<!-- ngRepeat: article in vm.contextData.similar --><div class="doc-all-related-articles-list-item ng-scope" ng-repeat="article in vm.contextData.similar"> 
			<a ng-href="/document/1589116" title="RFID security and privacy: a research survey" target="_self" href="/document/1589116">
				<span ng-bind-html="::(vm.contextData.isStandard ? article.standardNumber + ' - ' + article.title : article.title) | charlimitHtml:185" mathjax-bind="" class="ng-binding">RFID security and privacy: a research survey</span>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

optimized especially for the inkjet printing process. These tags are printed using narrow conductors, which enables low cost and fast manufacturing rate. We have manufactured such tag designs using three different line widths: 50, 125, and 200 &amp;#x03BC;m. In this letter, we present the simulation and measurement results. We have also included a comparison between the novel narrow-line tag and a dipole-type commercial tag. Results are encouraging; the read range of the narrow-line tag is comparable to the read range of the commercial tag even though the commercial tag is made of copper, which has approximately two times higher conductivity than the silver ink used in this study.
